English

The delusion that the soul is nothing but the body and the senses (prakс╣Ыti)
disappears when one has a knowledge of the distinctive features of sentient beings and non-sentient things.
So also the disputes on such questions as the unity of the j─лva and God will no longer continue,
when the characteristic features of each of them are marked out.
Our ─Бc─Бrya-s, whose wisdom never failed,
teach us about the existence of three realities (Tattvas)
classified in the s’─Бstr─Бs as the experiencing subjects (bhokt─Б), the objects of experience and enjoyment (bhogyam)
and He who rules over both of them (I┼Ыvara).

English

It may be asked -

why the ─Бc─Бryas should state that the three tatv─Бs or ‘reals’ should be specially prescribed for the study of those who seek mokс╣гa , when they form only a part of the six things that should be known, namely, the five truths arthapa├▒caka and the relationship of soul and body (which exists between God and the world)?

The answer is as follows:

It is necessary to root out the delusion that the body is the atma and that the j─лva is independent (of the Lord), as well as the view that there is no God, which is the cause of that delusion, for these are great obstacles to mokс╣гa.

it is revealed to the self by a part of it.

The luminosity of attributive knowledge is obstructed at the time

рдиреАрд▓рдореЗрдШрдГ (рд╕рдВ)

рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪреЛрджреНрдпрдореН рдЕрдкрд┐,
рдзрд░реНрдо-рднреВрдд-рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди–рдзрд░реНрдорд┐-рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирдпреЛрд░реН рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╡реИрд╖рдореНрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдмрдиреНрдзреА-рдХреГрддреНрдп
рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдг-рдмрд▓реЗрди рдкрд░рд┐рд╣реГрддрдореН ред

English

It may be asked :-

" How could there be, in a luminous object (viz. s’uddhasattvam),
qualities like form and taste
and classifications like earth and water and also modifications.
Self luminous things like the soul and attributive knowledge do not, in general,
have shape, taste, smell and the like)”?

The answer is as follows:-
(All self-luminous objects are not alike
but have differences peculiar to each);
for example, knowledge or self which is the substrate (i.e. the soul) and attributive knowledge,
though both are luminous,
are different from each other in other respects.

Knowledge, which is the substrate, has subjectivity,
while attributive knowledge is objective, and apprehends objects.
So this objection can be given a counter-check (pratibandhi)
and cannot hold good in a matter where the authority of the ┼Ы─Бstra must be accepted.

and ┼Ъr─л kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa (Kannan) the object of description in the Veda,
is endowed with these and protects all from the top of Hastigiri.

“O, Sovereign of 30 ┼Ъr─лraс╣Еga!
As the Supreme V─Бsudeva (Para) endowed with all the six qualities,
you are the object of blissful enjoyment for those that have attained mokс╣гa ;
as Saс╣Еkarс╣гaс╣Зa being endowed with strength and knowledge,
you destroy the Universe and also promulgate the ┼Ы─Бstras;
as Pradyumna being endowed with lordship and virility,

as Aniruddha being endowed with splendour and the power to overcome others,
you protect the world and teach the Truth.
In this way you divide yourself.”

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдЧреГрд╣реАрддрд╛ рдЕрднрд╡рдиреН ред

English

The differences arising from planes like the waking state
have been thus summarised :-

“O Lord, 31 of 32 those that meditate on Thee,
some are like those in the waking state,
some like those that dream in sleep,
others like those that sleep without dreams,
and others still are like those that have fallen into a swoon.
(In the first group, the senses function,
in the second the senses do not function,
only the mind is active;
in the third group even the mind does not function; they only breathe;
in the fourth group even the breath is suspended).
In the same way, O Lord, Thou art in four forms
and dividest Thyself into four forms
and art meditated upon with attributes and weapons suited to each.”

Espa├▒ol

The differences arising from planes like the waking state
have been thus summarised :-

“O Lord, [^es37] of those that meditate on Thee,
some are like those in the waking state,
some like those that dream in sleep,
others like those that sleep without dreams,
and others still are like those that have fallen into a swoon.
(In the first group, the senses function,
in the second the senses do not function,
only the mind is active;
in the third group even the mind does not function; they only breathe;
in the fourth group even the breath is suspended).
In the same way, O Lord, Thou art in four forms
and dividest Thyself into four forms
and art meditated upon with attributes and weapons suited to each.”

рдореВрд▓рдореН

рдЬрд╛рдЧреНрд░рджрд╛рджрд┐рднреЗрджрдЩреНрдЧрд│рд┐рд▓реБрд│реНрд│ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдЩреНрдЧрд│реЖрд▓реНрд▓рд╛рдореН тАЬрдЬрд╛рдЧреНрд░рддреНрд╕реНрд╡рдкреНрдирд╛рддреНрдпрд▓рд╕рддреБрд░реАрдпрдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрдзреНрдпрд╛рддреГрдХреНрд░рдорд╡рджреБрдкрд╛рд╕реНрдпрдГ ред рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрддреНрддрджреНрдЧреБрдгрдкрд░рд┐рдмрд░реНрд╣рд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреБрд░реНрд╡реНрдпреВрд╣рдВ рд╡рд╣рд╕рд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдзрд╛тАЭ (рд░рдЩреНрдЧрд░рд╛рдЬрд╕реНрддрд╡рдореН рдЙрддреНрддрд░рд╢рддрдХрдореН - 40.) рдОрдгреНрдбреНрд░реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреГрд╣реАрддрдЩреНрдЧрд│рд╛рдпрд┐рдЯреНрд░реБ.

English - VI┼Ъ─АKHASTAMBHA

APPENDIX ( Chapter V Page 65 )

THE VI┼Ъ─АKHASTAMBHA AS DESCRIBED IN THE SATVATA SAMHIT─А AND THE LAKс╣вM─к TANTRA.

In the region of eternal glory (nitya vibh┼лti),
there is a huge column constituted of ┼Ыuddhasattvam.
It is a special form in which Bhagav─Бn appears there.
This column or pillar is called Vi┼Ы─Бkha y┼лpa.
The column consists of four parts called, respectively, j─Бgrat, (the waking state ), svapna (the dream ), suс╣гupti (dreamless sleep) and tur─лya (the fourth stage, counting from below upwards).

In the part called j─Бgratsthana,
which is somewhere above the base of the column,
there are four divine forms on the four sides called, respectively, V─Бsudeva, Saс╣Еkarс╣гaс╣Зa, Pradyumna and Aniruddha facing the east, the south the west and the north and shining like branches around that part of the column.
This collection of four forms is called J─Бgratvyuha.
The activity of this vynha is the creation, maintenance and destruction of the world.
The four forms are bright in colours, white, red and the like.
They have also arms or weapons.

Above this part of the column is the part called svapnasth─Бna.
Here, too, there are four divine forms V─Бsudeva, Saс╣Еkarshna, Pradyumna and Aniruddha
shining like branches, as before, to the east, the south, the west and the north.
This collection of four vyuhas in the second part of the column from below is called svapnavyuha.
These four forms have no activities like creation and maintenance,
but have only the will to do so.
Their colours, too, are not so bright as those of the lower vy┼лha.
They have weapons
but no banners and other accessories.

Above the svapnasthana, which is the second part from below,
is the third part or sth─Бna called suс╣гuptisth─Бna.
Here too there are four divine forms with the same names as in the two other parts already described
and in the same order.
This collection of four forms is called suс╣гuptivyuha.
These forms have neither activities
nor even the will or the desire to act.
They have just the experience of their own bliss and nothing else.

In the form of V─Бsudeva
which is like a branch of the column shooting on the eastern side,
there is no such thing as a body with limbs and the like
and it shines with all the six qualities.
The other three forms, Saс╣Еkarс╣гaс╣Зa and the like on the other three sides
have a body with hands, feet and the like.
But they have no weapons;
on the palms they bear lines resembling the conch, and the weapons.
These forms have no colours.

The uppermost or fourth part of the column (Tur─лya sth─Бna) has also similar four forms with the same names as in the former parts.
This collection of four is the Tur─лya vy┼лha.
They have no bodies with limbs and the like
but resemble the V─Бsudeva form of the suс╣гupti vy┼лha.
They have no activities, no will, no weapons and no lines on the palm resembling arms.
All the six qualities shine in the form called V─Бsudeva
and the other three have, each, only two of these qualities.

The names j─Бgrat, svapna, suс╣гupti and tur─лya are given to them on the analogy of these states in man in the ordinary world,
according to the greater or the lesser activity found in each.
The tur─лya state is like that in a swoon when even the breath is suspended,
whereas in the suс╣гupti state, the man just breathes in or breathes out;
in the svapna, his external senses cease to act, only the mind is active,
in the j─Бgrat state, both the mind and the external senses act.

These four parts with four vy┼лhas in each
correspond to the four stages of development
that may be found in the worshipper who meditates on them.

On the lowest stage of meditation,
there is no full control of the external senses and the mind;

in the second stage of development,
control of the external senses has been attained
but not of the mind;

in the next stage,
the mind, too, has been controlled
and the man who meditates is seen just breathing in and breathing out
with no other activity or sign of life;

in the last or perfect development of meditation,
he is like one in a swoon, not even breathing in or out.

рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕-рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ

рдХреЗрд╢рд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдЧрд│реН рдЖрди рдкрдиреНрдиреН-рдЗрд░рдгреНрдбреБ рд░реВрдкрдЩреНрдЧрд│реН рдЙрдореН рд╡реНрдпреВрд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд│реН.

рдиреАрд▓рдореЗрдШрдГ (рд╕рдВ)

рдХреЗрд╢рд╡рд╛рджреАрдирд┐ рджреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╢ рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгреНрдпрдкрд┐ рд╡реНрдпреВрд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ ред

English

The twelve forms that begin with Ke┼Ыava are other forms derived from the vy┼лhas.

Espa├▒ol

The twelve forms that begin with Ke┼Ыava are other forms derived from the vy┼лhas.

38 " Having shaped a beautiful image of Viс╣гс╣Зu
with a lovely face and lovely eyes,
out of gold, silver and the like
in a manner that would be pleasing,
one should adore it, bow to it,
sacrifice to it and meditate on it.

which is none other than Brahman
and will have all one’s sins dispelled.”

рдореВрд▓рдореН (рддре░рдкре░)

рддреЗрд▒рд╡рд┐рдпрдореНрдмрд┐рдирд░реН рд╕рд┐рддреНрддреБрдорд╕рд┐рддреНрддреБрдорд┐рд▒реИрдпреБрдореЖрди
рд╡реЗрд▒реБрдмрдбреБрдореН рд╡рд┐рдпрдгреНрдбреНрд░рддреНрддреБрд╡рдореВрдгреНрдбреНрд░реБрдореН рд╡рд┐рдиреИрдпреБрдбрдореНрдмрд┐рд▓реН
рдХреВрд▒реБрдмрдбреБрдЩреН рдЧреКрдбреБрдореЛрдЧрдореБрдиреН рджрд╛рдирд┐рд▒реИрдпрд╛рдЩреНрдЧреБрд▒рд┐рдкреНрдкреБрдореН
рдорд╛рд▒ рдирд┐рдиреИрдиреНрджрд░реБрд│рд╛рдиреН рдорд▒реИрдиреВрд▓реНрджрдиреНрдж рд╡рд╛рджрд┐рдпрд░реЗ. (12)

рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕-рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ (рд╕рдВре░рдкре░)

рдЖрд╡рд╛рдкреЛрджреНрд╡рд╛рдкрддрд╕реН рд╕реНрдпреБрдГ рдХрддрд┐ рдХрддрд┐ рдХрд╡рд┐-рдзреА-рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рд╡рддреН рддрддреН-рддрджреН-рдЕрд░реНрдереЗрд╖реНрд╡реН,
рдЖрдирдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐-рдирд╛рд╕реНрддреНрдпреЛрд░реН, рдЕрдирд╡рдзрд┐-рдХреБрд╣рдирд╛-рдпреБрдХреНрддрд┐-рдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд╛рдГ рдХреГрддрд╛рдиреНрддрд╛рдГ ред
рддрддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдХрд╕реН рддреБ рд▓реЛрдкреНрддреБрдВ рдкреНрд░рднрд╡рддрд┐ рд╕рд╣рд╕рд╛ рдирд┐рд╕реНрд╕рдорд╕реНрддрд╛рдиреН рд╕рдорд╕реНрддрд╛рдиреН
рдкреБрдВрд╕реНрддреНрд╡реЗ рддрддреНрддреНрд╡реЗрди рджреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗ, рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЕрдкрд┐ рди рдЦрд▓реБ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рддрд╛ +++(рд╢рд░реАрд░реЗ/рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реЗ)+++ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдгреБрддрд╛-рдзреАрдГ рее резрел рее

English

By the addition of a point here
and the omission of a point there,
there are countless systems of thought,
each appearing beautiful with fallacious arguments
owing to the endless differences due to ‘is’ and ‘is not’.
These are indeed as numerous as the poems
composed by the imagination of poets
(some omitting an incident
and others inventing an incident and so forth).
Notwithstanding this,
the unparalleled vision of the truth (about the tattvas) will make them all vanish at once into thin air.
When the man is seen in reality,
the delusion that he is an animal or a log of wood, sth─Бс╣Зu vanishes at once.

So also when, with the help of the pram─Бс╣Зas, Puruс╣гottama is ascertained as the Supreme Deity,
the delusion that Rudra (Sth─Бс╣Зu) or any other is the Supreme Deity is at once dispelled.

Espa├▒ol

By the addition of a point here
and the omission of a point there,
there are countless systems of thought,
each appearing beautiful with fallacious arguments
owing to the endless differences due to ‘is’ and ‘is not’.
These are indeed as numerous as the poems
composed by the imagination of poets
(some omitting an incident
and others inventing an incident and so forth).
Notwithstanding this,
the unparalleled vision of the truth (about the tattvas) will make them all vanish at once into thin air.
When the man is seen in reality,
the delusion that he is an animal or a log of wood, sth─Бс╣Зu vanishes at once.

So also when, with the help of the pram─Бс╣Зas, Puruс╣гottama is ascertained as the Supreme Deity,
the delusion that Rudra (Sth─Бс╣Зu) or any other is the Supreme Deity is at once dispelled.

рдореВрд▓рдореН (рд╕рдВре░рдкре░)

рдЖрд╡рд╛рдкреЛрджреНрд╡рд╛рдкрддрд╕реНрд╕реНрдпреБрдГ рдХрддрд┐рдХрддрд┐ рдХрд╡рд┐рдзреАрдЪрд┐рддреНрд░рд╡рддреНрддрддрджрд░реНрдереЗрд╖реНрд╡реН

рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╕-рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ

рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрд░рд╣рд╕реНрдпрддреНрд░рдпрд╕рд╛рд░реЗ

рд╢реНрд░реАрдорддреЗ рдирд┐рдЧрдорд╛рдиреНрддрдорд╣рд╛рджреЗрд╢рд┐рдХрд╛рдп рдирдордГ рее

рдореВрд▓рдореН

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдХрд╡рд┐рддрд╛рд░реНрдХрд┐рдХрд╕рд┐рдВрд╣рд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдиреНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рддрдиреНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп
